RATING: 10
Without a doubt one of the best games I own, including the sister game and all add-ons. This game has a simple basic rule-set but the cards provide variety. While other games have variety from game to game, Dominion almost seems like a different game every time you play. Critical thinking skills are both demanded and exercised by this game. The wording on the cards is clear and precise and requires players to have similar thinking to play. I generally use this game as a litmus test to see if others can think precisely, cleverly and deviously (as opposed to thinking fuzzy and using language lazily).

After countless games, this one has dropped a little.  It's now in the realm of "fun to play" but never do I look forward to playing.  Still enjoyable though.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The cards added in Intrigue put a twist on my favorite deckbuilder.  I like the multitype cards and how some cards utilize that well such as "Tribute" which makes the player to the left of the user discard the top 2 cards from his/her deck and rewards the user depending on how many different types of cards are discarded; an action card gives +2 actions, a treasure card +2$, and a victory card +2 cards.  The victory point cards with other uses also make the game more interesting.  This expansion adds quite a bit of fun variety and makes several new engines possible.

RATING: 9
This expansion is more like "Dominion: Round Two."  The new cards are *extremely* nice.  Possibly overpowering in a few respects, but they shore up some of the weaknesses in the base game.  I like how they mix up the gameplay and change things.  The combo cards (VP + something else) are very nice, while the new attack cards are just mean!  Best effect likely obtained by mixing this with the first/base game.

Still not deep or strategic enough for me to rate a 10.  Can be pretty random and unforgiving.

Some of the cards in this expansion flat out improve on cards in the base set with the most notable one being the Ironworks vs. the Workshop.  Why would I bother with the Workshop ever again?  The expansion totally outmodes some base cards and that doesn't strike me as a good thing nor as a good game model.

An excellent game that is well worth playing.  I like this one better than the base game.  Improves on it in almost every respect.  People new to this "series" should probably start with the base game as it is simpler and, more likely, easier to follow.  For those of us experienced with the base game, this expansion simply rocks!

I was initially skeptical and preferred Dominion cards, but once I got used to the Intrigue cards, I think that they offer more variety.

RATING: 3
Pretty generic like the core set but with worse cards. Essentially just a less interesting Prosperity. The only real notable non-vanilla things are Duke with Dutchies, especially if you have the Dutchess card in your collection.

Overall, it's further plagued by my major point against Dominion: EVERYONE HAS ACCESS TO THE SAME EXACT STRATEGIES. Meaning if you find a good Harem strategy which gets countered and you counter that then everyone counters the counter and it fucking never ends. The only safe thing is to again, ignore the Kingdom stock and just buy money. Except it's worse in this expansion for two reasons:

1. There are even MORE self-countering strategies
2. All the cards are walls of text and more complicated which means it takes a lot more work for actually less impact.

Just avoid this piece of shit.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Player: 2-4
Time: 30mins

In Dominion: Intrigue (as with Dominion), each player starts with an identical, very small deck of cards. In the center of the table is a selection of other cards the players can "buy" as they can afford them. Through their selection of cards to buy, and how they play their hands as they draw them, the players construct their deck on the fly, striving for the most efficient path to the precious victory points by game end.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Simply superb!  Over 60 plays...

Adds so much dimension to the original.  Probably not quite as easily accessible for new players, but for those familiar with Dominion already, this is just the ticket.

So many more options available and decisions to make.  The game really feels a lot more interactive.

The fact that you can mix and match with the base set offers even wider possibilities and many, many more enjoyable games.

Dominion itself has been an enormous hit with all my friends, and Intrigue is proving it's worth even more so.

If you like Dominion, I would heartily recommend Intrigue, as it adds so much extra flavour and extensibility to the original game.  

A definite 11 out of 10 for me.

Kellemes meglepetés! Az alapjátékra néhány játszma után ráuntunk, nagyon lapos volt. Ebben az újabb változatban megjelenik néhány olyan lap, ami kicsit több taktikai lehetőséget nyújt, gondolok itt pl. a Herceg kártyára, ami a pontozást teszi színesebbé.
Egyébként maga a játék egy nagy lenyúlás, a lapoknak kb. a fele ugyanaz, mint ami az alapjátékban volt, jobb helyeken ezt kiegként adnák ki. Többek közt ezért nem is vettem meg. A BGG-n eleinte nem is került fel önálló játékként, aztán pár héten át hol önálló játékként szerepelt, hol kiegként. Ennyi erővel bármelyik power grid pályához adhatnának játékpénzt és bábúkat, és mind szerepelhetne önálló játékként.
De a lenyúlás ellenére is az alapjátéknál jobb mindenképp!
---
Elég sok kártyán lehet akár 3-4 dolog közül is választani, ez tetszik. Ami még érdekes, hogy bizonyos kártyakombináció esetén akár olyan stratégiát is lehet játszani, ami egyáltalán nem igényel kincsvásárlást (legalábbis nem a klasszikus réz-ezüst-aranyat). Egyértelműen változatosabb az alapjátéknál!

RATING: 10
My favourite Dominion part so far. It was incredible to play this after playing over 70 games of the base game - it really brought up the idea to a whole new level. I love the fact that there are much more choices in the game. You not only choose what to buy but you also have several options to play an action card. I love the victory/action or victory/treasure cards. I love the fact that the rule from the base game (who first buys gold wins) is much more rare with the expansion. I love cards like Courtyard which allow you to decide if you want your current turn to be as good as possible or do you want to make your chances bigger to have a great next turn.

RATING: 7
Initial Impression: This is a great gateway game, being very easy to teach and learn. The number of cards in the set make for a lot of variability. The Intrigue set allows for some direct interaction and nastiness. This is a perfect game to showcase the deckbuilding mechanism.

10 Plays: Coming back to this game after a long hiatus, the game feels cozy, comforting, and familiar, like an old, favorite sweater. With only 10 games under our belt we haven't even begun to explore all the different combinations of cards. We've experimented with a few strategies but found that the cards on the table will dictate the winning strategy for that session. I can see this game staying in our collection for a while.

RATING: 7
Dominion was the first game I purchased after discovering BGG.com and Dicetower.com  Between Tom Vasel's reviews and praise of the game, its high ranking on the BGG charts, and my search for a game that I could play well for 2 players (my wife being the 2nd player), this game looked like a home run.  It turns out it was a Grand Slam.  My wife really likes card games (like Bridge, Cribbage, etc.) so this wasn't such a far stretch in that there would still be cards in your hand.  I like customizable card games so it seemed like a fitting game.  In the summer of 2011 we played this game every day during our then 18 mo. old daughter's nap.  I got so addicted that I went and grabbed Dominion (the original game) and Prosperity.  Though the novelty has worn off and my rating of the game has fallen from a 9.5 to an 8 (edited 2.8.12) it still stands as a wonderful game to introduce to people who like gaming and non-gamers alike.  The game mechanics are easy to master and it plays quickly once everyone has a feel for the 10 Kingdom cards that are in play.

RATING: 10
What makes Dominion one of my favorite games is the variety, and this expansion adds tons of that.  It also adds some fresh money/victory cards which is a treat as well.  And, thanks to this expansion, I finally got hooked.  I found myself dying to play another game of Dominion as soon as I finished the last one.  I actually have passed up on playing games that I really enjoy, or even the opportunity to play new games, just so I could play more Dominion.  Call it addiction if you want, but I am having so much fun with this particular addiction.

Some of the fun in this expansion is in the cards that give added value to some of the less important cards.  Suddenly a Coppersmith makes Coppers something desireable, or a Duke makes Duchies almost as useful as a Province.  And the added interaction is a treat as well.  If I were to level a complaint against this expansion it would be that the choice cards can sometimes slow down players who have analysis-paralysis.  Still the added variety is delightful, and I will always have these cards in the mix when I'm randomly selecting kingdom cards for a game.

RATING: 5
This is (supposedly) the "player interaction" set.  I find it only moderately succeeds at this.  Most of the interaction cards are underpowered (Minion, Masquerade, Scout, Secret Chamber ...) and thus just get passed up all the time.  Most other cards are just average in power, a few highlights (Saboteur, Torturer - all attack cards, hmm) , but Intrigue cards are more likely to fade in the background if there is a power card on the table.  Also, Coppersmith?  Really?

It does have enough variety to make it worthwhile if you play a lot of Dominion (I do).  However, you should purchase Seaside first, and then move on to this if you still get a lot of play.

---
Early days, but so far I'm pretty impressed with the new Dominion set - it really does have a different feel from the classic, and it almost feels like it plays better. A little worried by the complexities of some of the cards, since Dominion is  a game that really needs to be played fast. But the new card combinations (action/VP, money/VP) are particularly welcome and can change up the pace and so the desirable deck mixes. New combinations are obviously welcome. I'm not exactly sure how far this particular train goes and how much it can really be milked - I doubt very much more, and too many expansions could very easily strangle the game - but so far so good.

I am rather irritated that RGG did not take the opportunity to upgrade the thoroughly mediocre physical design on this game. Text is still to small, iconography is poor, and it's idiotic that the treasures and VPs all have identical designs (sure, keep the highlight and text box colors to indicate category, but make the coin and background colors distinct). The contrast between Race for the Galaxy and Dominion is stark.

RATING: 7.5
A great improvement over the original - which didn't even need improved.

This expansion adds an entirely different dimension to the game, as many of the cards force you to actually make decisions (such as the Pawn, Nobles, or Minion).  As such, it also increases the player interaction a bit more with the attacks cards.

By the way, I think Tribute is broken by not being listed as an "Attack" card since it mills your draw deck for 2 cards - not fair, and I should have the option to be able to respond with a Secret Chamber/Moat.  If the Bureaucrat is an "Attack" then so should Tribute.

RATING: 9

We played the base game 50+ times, and Prosperity almost 40 times (though most plays combine sets), so I'm not terribly worried about whether or not we'll get our money's worth out of this purchase.

RATING: 6
Slightly more complex than the original Dominion, Intrigue adds significantly more interactions to the game and spruces up formerly lackluster strategies.  I'm not sure that it's better than Dominion as a stand-alone game, but it's worth owning both Dominion and Intrigue.  Really worth it.  It's still the cheapest, quickest, and most elegant CCG experience without actually playing a CCG.

A significant bonus is the ability to play with more than four players if you own both Dominion and Intrigue.  I've played with 3-6 players, and it's great in all cases - though the tempo changes slightly, it's still far from a slow game!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
I haven't played a lot of D:I, but I have played enough Dominion to know what I think of the basic concept here, and it's solid enough, but attack cards are generally my least favorite thing in Dominion (slow the game down and make it more confrontational than I like when there are more than 1 in the mix) and this set has a number of them.

On the positive end of things, there seem to be a higher density of cards that have decision points involved, on the downside, many of these cards are attack cards and the Dominion universe still does not have cards that adequately punish the playing of attack cards; I'm waiting for something that allows you to search the offending player's hand and force them to trash something of your choice, or something that doesn't allow them to buy anything for the round or the like.

Some of the attack cards in this are onerous to deal with because they change the composition of your deck, particularly Swindler. There are now additional ways to sift junk out of your deck as well, but I still find it annoying.

On the balance, there is a decent mix of new stuff here. On the main I prefer the original card mix to this (and greatly prefer the original + Prosperity when I'm in the mood for a slightly longer game). If you're getting this as an expansion only it's certainly a nice thing to have as you will be able to more effectively tailor the game to your liking. Just don't make the godawful mistake of playing the game with too many attack cards, it will slow the thing down to a crawl.

The 4 here reflects the fact that I find this slightly worse than the base game by itself. It's not terrible, and I would be willing to play it, but I would lobby for other options.

- straight Dominion (I won)
- straight Intrigue (he won)

- random where there were more Intrigue (he won)
- exactly 1/2 and 1/2 (I won)

RATING: 7
A lot of new cards here, and that provides variety to those bored with the base game (as I was for quite awhile).  The big plus to me here is that several cards add to the interaction level, making it less of multi-player solitaire.  This game needed that badly, in my opinion.  Few of these interactive cards are devastating - they just are annoying and can thwart someone's short-term plans.

Although I can see the marketing value of making this game playable on its own, I think it lacks balance and is improved by having some base game cards that are simpler.

So far my preference on expansions goes to Seaside, which offers more interesting choices.  Still, this is a nice solid expansion.

RATING: 7
I don't know that you'll go wrong getting this over the base set if you're picking one or the other. This one adds options to your choices. You get to choose one of three options and things like that. I prefer the base set over this, but it's still fun. I've taught people Dominion via this set and with the base set, and the base set is always the way to go. Choices are nice, but if you're new to Dominion or deck building, the choices get to be overwhelming.

Some of the art is confusing if you care about that. Some of it looks really sharp, but then some cards look more cartoonish. Not sure why the difference.

Overall, it's worth having in your Dominion collection as an additional set. If you're just starting out and you haven't played the game, I would recommend the base set first.

RATING: 9
[2009-09-14 Rating: n.a. -> 9]
All in all, Dominion: Intrigue is a nice addition to the Dominion-family. Somehow it doesn't really grab me like the base-game, but I haven't played it even remotely as often as vanilla Dominion. Since most of my games are with my girlfriend and she doesn't really enjoy the game when it is played too cut-throat, I guess I haven't even started to explore the full potential of the new cards yet.

* There seems to be more interaction due to the cards of this expansion. But since a good deal of the cards from this expansion can potentially mess up the cards of the other players, the game loses a bit of it's friendliness. This is something I don't mind. But similar to my girlfriend, there are people who don't like this quality in a game. So I guess, you have to be a little careful not to scare people away by adding this expansion.

* The new double-function cards are a great addition. I do especially like the Noble-card.

RATING: 7
Follow up game to the excellent Dominion.  Players start with a 10 card deck of crappy copper and estates, and must sculpt a game winning deck stuffed full of victory points.  You get a bit wary of expansions to blockbusters, but this one is great.  Basically a self contained game that can integrate with the base game.  Played three games of the new one and like the branching decision tree that the new cards offer (the OR option).  Still plays like lightning once you know what the cards do.  The Bridge seems amazingly good, but not a game breaker.  Zero theme, but good game play.  Again, crappy cards with too small text, but I guess we're committed to this look now.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.75
(Up from 7.5 base game)
Intrigue improves on the basic dominion formula in a number of ways.  First, there are cards which have 2 or more types, an obvious but still welcome introduction.  Then there are cards which have multiple functions, and the player decides which to use each time it's played.  Lastly, there are just more complex types of effects and interactions.  This makes it a more tactical and competitive version of the game.  As the first of the expansions, it started to show us what could be done with the design space carved out, yet unexplored, by the original.  

This is as good a spot as any to put a word on player counts.  The base game plays well with 2, 3, or 4.  The expansion includes enough starting deck cards and extra victory cards to play with 5.  DON'T.  
There aren't any more of each kingdom card in the supply, so your strategy is heavily restricted by what the other players are doing.  And more players just means longer to get back to you and more waiting for people to shuffle.  If you have 6, I suggest you do what our group does and set up two 3-person tables with different card sets, play separately, then switch.  If you have 5, play something else.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

An interesting expansion of the dominion universe. Better than the base, because of the expanded possibilities - but the potential for draggy end game turns and burnout tempers my views on the game. Good here and there - can't play it too many times in a row though.

RATING: 6
Played this as a stand-alone for a couple of rounds to try out the new cards. This expansion contains just a little too much bizarro to really be fun on its own. Both my wife and I have found that this version really works much better when used in conjunction with the original game. It keeps the games fresh and exciting with the new and interesting dynamics without overwhelming the gamer with too many strange mechanics. Good expansion to a great game, but the base game is a must own, imo.

RATING: 8.5
Dominion is easily my favorite game of all my collection. It is the game all deck-buildings games wish they were. I have to say that I am not an enthusiast of card games (I'm more of a boardgame gamer myself), but this one is simply fantastic. There is not that much luck, and a lot of strategy, all packed in a thirty-40 minute game. 
Then why do I only give it an 8.5? Because you will get tired of it if you only have one box. You need at least 2.5 boxes (there are small expansions) for it to get real sweet. Although the boxes will start taking a lot of space, and it is a bit cumbersome to carry. Try any of the good ideas given by other bgg'ers!
Dominion intrigue is one of the two stand-alone Dominions, and it is clearly more replayable than the base set, which is pretty straigt-forward as far as strategies go.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Dominion, 2008
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
In Dominion: Intrigue (as with Dominion), each player starts with an identical, very small deck of cards. In the center of the table is a selection of other cards the players can "buy" as they can afford them. Through their selection of cards to buy, and how they play their hands as they draw them, the players construct their deck on the fly, striving for the most efficient path to the precious victory points by game end.

From the back of the box: "Something’s afoot. The steward smiles at you like he has a secret, or like he thinks you have a secret, or like you think he thinks you have a secret. There are secret plots brewing, you’re sure of it. At the very least, there are yours. A passing servant murmurs, “The eggs are on the plate.” You frantically search your codebook for the translation before realizing he means that breakfast is ready. Excellent. Everything is going according to plan."

Dominion: Intrigue adds rules for playing with up to 8 players at two tables or for playing a single game with up to 6 players when combined with Dominion. This game adds 25 new Kingdom cards and a complete set of Treasure and Victory cards. The game can be played alone by players experienced in Dominion or with the basic game of Dominion.

RATING: 10
(Note that these comments refer to the first edition of Intrigue, which came with a full set of Treasure and Victory cards, plus all the other core components. If you're new to Dominion now, you'll want the want the [thing=209418]second edition core set[/thing] before getting [thing=209419]the new Intrigue[/thing], which is purely an expansion.)

The core set is great, but it was Intrigue that made me a Dominion fan for life. I love the cards that give you a choice of effect (the Minion, etc.), as well as Victory cards that can actually be used for things (e.g., the Noble and the Harem). I think I actually prefer Intrigue to the original set, although the latter is still the place to start.

We've played one 6-player game, and it was fine. This is an easy enough game that you can't slow it down too much. Still, 2-4 players remains the sweet spot.

Recorded plays are for games using only Intrigue cards, recommended sets from the Intrigue rules, and for 5-6 player games.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.75
See Dominion for more background. This expansion strikes me as, literally, "intriguing." The extra player interaction with the new cards takes care of one of my "sadnesses" (I can't say gripes) with Dominion - that buying money tends to be more important than buying the action cards. It also makes the game take longer. I really hate the Swindler card, but I've got a whole forum thread about that. 

Overall, I find that using this expansion in combination with the original Dominion is the way to go. If they were one game together, I'd probably rate them a 9.25.

RATING: 6
First - why are my comments and plays here, rather than on Dominion proper?  Well, that's because my son owns the original.  Granted, at the time of this writing he is 12, but eventually he will go away to college and take his games with him.  D:I, on the other hand, is my game.

Dominion is a great game. It has its interactions without being too confrontational.  The card play combinations are very interesting, and with several more kingdom cards in the box than are used in any one game, the replayability is high.

A nine rating from me on this one is somewhat surprising.  I normally like very thematic games.  But where this game has almost no theme, it makes up for it in great play.

RATING: 7.2

I like Dominion, I find it to be quite a relaxing game. There are of course strategy to be had in there but it's not as taxing as many of the other games that I own. I'm a bit on the fence about Alchemy, given a choice I would probably have had the big box come with another expansion instead of that one.

It seems I only have two modes when it comes to this game; either I get obsessed with it and play it all the time or I'm annoyed with it because of stuff like "Big Money" etc and don't want to play it at all. Of all the games I own I think this one fluctuates the most in popularity.

Bought the update kits for basegame and Intrigue.

RATING: 3
Some people complain that the Dominion base set isn't interactive enough. That's certainly a point that is remedied by this expansion. It contains a lot of cards which directly impact other players' decks, usually not in a good way.

It looks like the target has been missed by a mile, though. If we had played a random setup and ended up with a bad mix that would at least be understandable. We did, however, play one of the recommended setups, and it was completely unplayable. No control whatsoever. If you were lucky you got to use a useful card once before it was downgraded, destroyed, stolen, or morphed into something completely different. Countermeasures were not available. Great fun. Not.

RATING: 7
As an expansion, Intrigue is great because it adds the much needed player interactions to the base game. Moreover, tougher tradeoffs have to be made by each player when certain cards are played.

When combined with the base set, Intrigue can allows up to 6 players in a single game.

The downside is that some of the new "attack" cards are way too chaotic and can totally mess up your plan. I think it is at the borderline of getting too random.

I prefer using Intrigue as an expansoin, adding a few Intrigue cards to the base set, rather than playing Inrigue as a standalone game. 

However, Intrigue does generate much more laughters than the basic Dominion.

Bottomline: more fun but less strategic.

RATING: 8.5
[b]Dominion Intrigue[/b] [i]Donald X Vacarinno 2009[/i]
A new Dominion version that is playable by itself, but an expansion at the same time (and honestly I think it shouldnt have the status of an independent entry in the ranks). Anyway, I think that Intrigue is a tad better than the core game in the meaning that it offers a more interactive and complex experience. But that also means complexity and thus more playing time and it is also a bit more unreacheable for the newbies. I recommend to play Dominion core game first and, if you like it, add later some Intrigue cards. In short, Intrigue is a game for the people that liked the core game and are willing to add some spice and interaction in their games. The cost is downtime, but I think it deserves a place on my shelves.

RATING: 8
Excellent strategic card game with quite low random chance.

Pros:
+ Many game starting set up combinations possible, 3'268'760 combinations to be precise,
+ Very high replay value,
+ Good mechanics, fast and easy game play - good playing time,
+ Simple rules, easy to get to play for beginners,
+ Aesthetics are good, cards are nice looking,
+ Cards powers are very well balanced.

Cons:
- Shuffling could be done differently, depending on player, some don't like to shuffle cards at all,
- Not easy to follow how other players are handling their cards.

RATING: 8
Note that I'm rating this as a Dominion expansion, not a standalone game.

I don't like the extreme randomness of the Saboteur.  If you want to buy a super-volatile card for yourself, that's fine.  But when you're doing it to someone else's deck, it can take some of the fun out of the game for many players.  Otherwise, this is a great set of cards that really fulfills the initial promise of Dominion.  Basic Dominion was all about which cards to purchase, with very few other decisions to be made.  With the addition of the Intrigue cards, players will often have interesting decisions to make during the actual card play.  That makes the game more satisfying for me.  Simply doubling the number of cards does a lot for Dominion, by creating a much broader array of novel and challenging card interactions.

RATING: 9
My first experience with it was with saboteur and swindler with newbies. The game took long time to finish and felt random. The reason behind this they did not play strategically and were not experienced gamers. I will never introduce those cards anymore. Like treasure map in seaside, the saboteur can strike very differently depending how the game turns out and it is hard to defend against it.

Generally, I like the cards in this set. The main game grew a little stale with the same combos all the time. New cards infused new strategies and many of these cards have options in it.

There is an option to play five or six player games and I have done that a few times, but nothing I really enjoy. You have to be more careful when having more players and choosing the kingdom cards, since some cards (especially attacks) can be quite powerful in this environment.

RATING: 7
Intrigue is okay.  I especially like the introduction of dual-type cards (Action/Victory cards are especially good).  Scout works well with Great Hall, Nobles, and even Harem, and would probably work well with other expansions with these dual-type cards.

Because there are a full set of Victory and Treasure cards in the box, it's possible to play with Intrigue and true expansions (without the base Dominion game).  In general, I'd say that the base game is better -- Village is better than Mining Village, and there's nothing as good as Market or Festival or even Chapel in this release.

Some cards give you many choices (like Pawn).  For only 2 coins, Pawn is quite a flexible and powerful card; with a +2 actions card like Shanty Town or Mining Village, the Pawn can be quite good (choose +1 Card, +1 Coin, for example).  However, this is actually a pain -- it's hard to keep track of what choices were used for each played instance of this type of card.

Intrigue has a bunch of vicious attack cards, and even cards that are not Attack cards (and so can't be defended against by a Blue card like Moat or Secret Chamber) but which still affect other players (like Masquerade).  One card is truly evil -- Saboteur.  I hate playing with this one -- it can unfairly attack a losing player who has barely managed to get enough treasure in a turn to get one Province in their deck, for example.  Maybe it should only be played with Remodel and Moat in play.

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is a great “expansion”.  Actually, it is probably not officially considered an expansion (since you can play it by itself without the original Dominion), but we treat as such, since it is essentially another (very nice) collection of additional cards.  It provides a variety  of new (25 or so action and victory) cards.  While I cannot think of any completely new concept they introduced with this expansion (like the “duration” mechanism introduced in Seaside), some of the cards provide more interaction with other players.  Some of the others provide a choice on what action(s) to take.  For example, Steward lets you choose one of the following:  (1) draw 2 extra cards, (2) receive 2 extra coin to go towards a purchase, or (3) trash 2 cards from your hand (handy for when you have curses).

And while there are few cards in the previous expansion (Seaside) that my family and I never choose (we have our own way of “randomizing” the 10 action piles), I cannot think of any card that does not get used at least every once in a while (although, now that I think about it, I suppose we rarely use “Shanty Town” and “Wishing Well” any more).

Oh, and there is one other benefit that I alluded to at the beginning.  This game comes with a new set of treasure and victory cards.  These are the same as what is included in the original Dominion game, but this is very nice as it provides a fresh set of these cards that get used (and worn down) often.

In any case, if you like original Dominion, I highly recommend adding Intrigue to your collection.

RATING: 7
Played it for the first time at a meetup tonight. Fascinating new cards to explore. Intrigue has a number of cards that allow more trashing, more interaction with the other players, and dual-purpose cards, such as victory+treasure or victory+action.

Because of these new cards, the game seems 'klunky'. It's not as smooth as the base game, or perhaps it is simply because it is my first game? We'll see how this grows on me over the coming weeks. Incidentally, the base game rarely comes out now.

Update (09/12/09) 5x F2F plays: Started random mixing of base and Intrigue cards, for slow introduction of Intrigue cards. Also played 5 Player game for first time.  5P game is admittedly longer, but still fun nonetheless. The new Intrigue cards cannot be ignored, as some of them are simply devastating. It's kind of like evolution: if you learn to use the new cards, they have a good chance of overtaking the old base cards. In the end, it is how one strings together dissimilar cards, or ignoring them completely, from the two sets to work together synergistically that causes a win or loss.

Update (10/24/09): An interesting thing about Dominion is that it is possible for several other players to join a 2-3 player game that just started, and has only gone 3-4 turns in. The late players are given the starting hand, plus a gold, and one or two silvers. This may give enough of boost to catch up with the other players. We have yet to work out the exact numbers, but the games have been close with this catch-up mechanism.

Update (11/28/09): First two-table 4P each session of Dominion+Intrigue, with four newbies. Went over well. First 6P game also. Length depends on type of kingdom cards--with Saboteur, Witch, and Tribute, game ended in 20 minutes with 4 piles emptying out. Scores ranged from -6 to 12 pts. Second 6P game lasted a bit longer. We even modified the ending rules by upping the condition to 5 piles, but this didn't matter. Still having difficulty mastering Intrigue cards, as they are constantly mixing with base cards (we don't play the preset layouts anymore), so this is frustrating. Because of this, Seaside may be my last expansion for a long time--I'm getting off that wagon.

Update (06/18/10): Downing this to a "7". See base game for explanation.

RATING: 7
Very much the same game, a mixed bag of enhancements. There are some more interesting cards this time, especially Nobles (hybrid Action/Victory card) and Harem (hybrid  Treasure/Victory). There is some rather game-jarring clunkiness in among the fresh ideas though, such as Swindler (other players trash the top card from their deck and you choose for them a card of equivalent value) and Saboteur (others turn over cards from their deck until they reach one costing 3+, trash it and choose another costing 2 less) which have the effect of substantially slowing down the game and rather defeat the purpose of a deck-builder, in my mind at least. A reasonable expansion, but some later ones are much better.

RATING: 7.86
Cartas con varios efectos a elegir uno.

Es un Dominon "Big Brother" para jugones. Casi una secuela más que una expansión porque reinventa el juego. Las decisiones ahora no están sólo en qué comprar (como en Dominion) sino que también aparecen en qué hacer con las cartas que ahora ofrecen varios efectos de los cuales habrá que elegir uno. Esto hace que la condición que aparecía en mis partidas de "gana el que consigue el primer oro" desaparezca en gran medida. Dura más, pero el juego es más dinámico y siempre se cuenta con el aliciente de tener un 5º o 6º jugador en la partida. Poco amigable con los novatos. PROS: cartas con opciones y más interactivas que eliminan la sensación de "solitario multijugador". CONS: añade más azar, caos y al juego y esto no gusta a todos. Sigue la estela de Magic (más combos gordos, usos alternativos en las cartas...). La interacción sigue siendo algo forzada. Sigue sin gustarme que las monedas tengan el mismo color y los PV's el mismo diseño con independencia de su valor. 

Con tantas expansiones, parece útil jugar con 3 ataques + 1 carta de victoria + 6 cartas de acción. Tantos ataques, dificultan mucho la estrategia big money. La carta de  victoria extra añade más profundidad y hace obligatorio pensar estrategias distintas. Las 6 acciones, mucha rejugabilidad.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
My favorite of the Dominion Expansions!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9

RATING: 7
A worthy addition to the base game, and can also be played standalone.  The cards follow a similar framework to the base cards, but some have more interesting effects.  Such as the Duke card which earns a victory point for every duchy in your deck, and the Baron card which allows you to utilise the Estate cards you have in your hand at the start of the game.

The 'Intrigue' part of the title seems to refer to the attacking cards in this expansion, none of which I am particularly find of.  One of them simply makes another player discard two cards - this is just annoying for the other players and often creates a long pause when the AP sets in.  I don't really enjoy this type of negative interaction and I much prefer the other cards that come in this generous addition to an already great game.

RATING: 9.5
2011-08-06

Initial Rating: 8.0 (August 2011)

When you have played Dominion a long time, patterns begin to emerge and one tends to follow the same paths as before. Enter Dominion: Intrigue. It adds a lot more possible card combinations and gives a lot of life to vanilla Dominion, all with very little extra complexity. It also offers a lot more interaction between players (which increases luck). If you like Dominion this is a must.

Without a doubt Dominion is the best deck building game out there.

I consider it a Dominion Expansion, not a standalone game.

I prefer to play this over the internet due to the constant shuffling.

Current Rating: 9.5
[hr]
2014-07-01

To this day, I continue to love Dominion. For me, it is still the king of the deckbuilders (many copycats didn’t grasp what made Dominion great), so it is no wonder than I like Dominion: Intrigue. I don’t have anything negative to say about the game. If someone pointed a gun to my head and made me find a flaw in the game it would be the card Saboteur. Perhaps the card I like the least in all the Dominion world. I found it amplifies the controlled luck to uncontrollable levels. I hate to play with it, but sometimes I do. I always play with random sets.

As I wrote before, Dominion is best if you can play it online (due to the shuffling), however I won’t say no to a game of Dominion (face to face or virtual). It’s a shame Goko didn’t deliver on its promises because this is the game I most want to play online on my iPad. Also I have bought all the physical cards and the virtual counterparts are very expensive on their website, so for now, I’m not playing online. 

For me Dominion is a two player game only. With more players the luck and the downtime begin to creep up to unmanageable levels.

One of 2009´s favorites.

Current Rating: 9.5
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The set appears more complex than the base game, which is a good thing.  I especially like the cards that combine card types, like the Harem and Great Hall, and the Duke which makes Duchies a viable primary path to victory.

Unfortunately the set adds two deck-destruction attacks, Saboteur and Swindler, which increases to three the number of Kingdom cards I'm not willing to play with.  That makes it more difficult to find a good game of Dominion in practice.

I probably won't be buying Intrigue though; the base game flamed out relatively quickly for me so I'm not eager to invest more money quite yet.  Perhaps if I didn't have to buy more treasure and victory point cards I might take the plunge.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
More than an expansion, it plays extremely well (equal to the original, IMO) as a stand-alone game.  "Fixes" the complaints on the original that there isn't enough interaction and that the play of the hand is automatic.

Interaction is the raison detre of this game, with the addition of 4 new attack cards, a new reaction card, and three other cards that are not attacks, but require actions from other players.  Also, many of these cards do much more to interfere not only with opponents' current or next turns, but also with the composition of their decks.

Hand play is also intensified with well over half of the cards requiring a choice to be made as part of card play, or requires a risk to be taken as part of the decision whether or not to play a card at all.

Increases the length of the game somewhat in proportion to the number of "Intrigue" cards included in a 10 card action deck, as many of the cards require thought to play and/or react to.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
[b][url=https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/448505/2009-golden-geek-nominees-announced-voting-open]2009 Golden Geek Nominee[/url][/b]

In Dominion: Intrigue, each player starts with an identical, very small deck of cards. In the center of the table is a selection of other cards the players can "buy" as they can afford them. Through their selection of cards to buy, and how they play their hands as they draw them, the players construct their deck on the fly, striving for the most efficient path to the precious victory points by game end.

Players:   2, 3, 4 (5, 6 with Dominion)
Time:      30 min
Mechanics:  [property=2041][/property], [property=2664][/property], [property=2040][/property]

[u]Integrations/Expansions[/u]

I think this makes for a good first expansion as it adds just the sort of decisions that the base game wanted more of, and many Intrigue cards feel like they have more use when you are playing with a higher proportion of other Intrigue cards.

RATING: 9.5
My favorite expansion so far.  It adds a lot of interesting Action cards, as well as making Victory cards useful, rather than just dead cards in hand.  For example, Baron turns Estate cards into an easy way to ramp up to eight money and purchase a Province.  There are also hybrid cards, like Great Hall, which is both an Action Card and a Victory Card, or Harem, which is a Victory Card and a Treasure card.

RATING: 8
Intrigue adds some interesting elements to the base game of Dominion.  However, considered on its own, it doesn't seem as balanced.  It has a lot of complex, slowing elements, as well as more randomizing effects.  Games can drag on quite a bit or finish up pretty rapidly (though not always predictably).  There are a lot of Intrigue-only setups that players will see and dread playing, which was a bit rarer with the base set.  Combined, the distribution is a bit better.

RATING: 8
A refreshing addition to Dominion, in terms of game mechanics.

Some cards lengthen the game, compared to the base game (Saboteur…), and, when present, they make the game drag too much, for us (the percentage of time spent thinking was too low, for a game that lasts as long as Race for the Galaxy).  However, most of the cards are not like this.

Downgraded to 9 because I find that Puzzle Strike has a few advantages over Dominion.

RATING: 8
Cards have a lot more text than the base game, making this less suitable as a gateway game. I feel like because the base set was simpler the cards in Intrigue take a little bit more finesse to use properly.

EDIT after playing all the other expansions: By itself, Intrigue feels kind of clunky to me. Base game's cards are much simpler yet seem to combo easier together, while Intrigue's seem like you need more pieces, while having more disruptive attacks and having a weaker reaction card to protect yourself. However, I have really liked how Intrigue has integrated with other sets. Unlike other sets who usually have cards that work well together and do a bit more poorly when diluted, Intrigue has cards that splash just as well within the expansion as out of. Also, the finesse needed to use the cards adds more tactical decisions in the game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
[microbadge=13167]

Many prefer this game to base Dominion, but I am not among them.  I do see the appeal in this game, and I do in fact like it a lot.  However, if you own only one Dominion, I would go with the original and treat Intrigue instead as an expansion (even if, you know, it isn't.)  What Intrigue does is it makes many of the tactical decisions more complex (fixing a complaint for many who felt that hands played themselves) and changes the victory conditions somewhat (not actually changing the rules, but you are far more likely to draw out with Intrigue than buy up the Provinces).  A good addition to to the series, but not a replacement core set.

This is one of my all time favourite games!

RATING: 7
Game in a Nutshell: Just like Dominion with all new cards to build your deck.

Played as: 4 player

Played with: Mixed in with base Dominion only.

Pros: Has most all the positives of the base game with the addition that I think the designer put some more effort into the decks having a stronger interactive element. Points go to the publisher also for choosing to make this a stand alone game by adding the appropriate cards needed to do so.

Cons: On the flip side, some of the simplicity of the base game was lost while coming up with ideas for new cards.

Other: If deciding one or the other between this and base Dominion, it's basically a little trade off of simple accessibility vs a bit more player interaction. Really, you couldn't go very wrong with either one and then there's always the option of having both.

Best Use: Grab if you want to play Dominion with a touch more interaction.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
The real challenge of Dominion lies in deciding which cards to buy.  But once you've bought them, the cards tend to play themselves.  There is little to actually think about when playing the hand you're dealt.

Intrigue adds a breath of fresh air with the mechanic of choice.  Cards may be played to give more cards, more actions, more buys, or sometimes a combination.  This makes each hand more flexible and can give cards extended life, as they have an important place in both the early and late game.  Great expansion.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[i]Play comments are listed under Dominion base game[/i]

01/12/2013: See my comments under the Dominion base game for my thoughts on the general gameplay and quality.

This is the only expansion I own, as of this writing.  It can be played alone though, as it does come with all of the standard money and victory point cards needed in any session of Dominion.

From my experience, Intrigue specifically address the lack of player interaction "issue" with the base set.  To me, it's not a big deal.  However, there are very few cards that directly involve the other players when using just the base set of cards.  Intrigue adds many, many cards that will interact with the other players on the table...discard cards, trash (discard permanently) cards, steal cards, etc.  If you want to have others involved more in your turn, then this is a good set to add to your Dominion set up.

However, depending on which Intrigue cards and how many there are compared to the number of base cards in the game, this could cause two things: play length can increase just because there is more going on each turn and you can lose any random card (including large victory points) due to just a random draw of your deck.  This can be a little frustrating when you have a "good" deck of cards that builds up your victory point total, and then because someone else played a card where you have to trash a card from your deck, 6VP are lost for no real reason.

Generally, we play with five random cards from each of the sets I have, and more often than not, things are fun and not too randomly decided.  But it does happen on occasion.  Overall, this is a good addition to the base as it adds even more variety and fun to a very solid game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
[url=http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/423502/dominion-intrigue-intriguingly-complex]Dominion: Intrigue Review: Intriguingly Complex?[/url]

This is the first expansion to [GAMEID=36218].  It is also listed as a stand alone game, which is why it has it's own ranking.  I really like intrigue because it gave me more desire to play dominion again.  I had 150+ plays and was starting to feel like I was playing the same game.  With intrigue there is a lot that mixed that up.

In intrigue, just as dominion, all players start with 7 copper cards, worth one coin each, and 3 estate cards, worth one vp each.  The object is to use the 10 kingdom cards in play to build the most efficient deck that will get you the most vps by the end of the game.  In dominion all vp cards were dead cards in your hand, but intrigue has added 4 different vp cards, 3 of which actually help you during the game, two of them are actions, and one of them is treasure.  The game comes with 25 kingdom cards, as does dominion, to choose your 10 from.  We usually do this randomly, and they have supplied one extra card for each deck to shuffle in order to do this.  They also have some pre-defined setups, or you can come up with any method you want for getting the 10 cards to play with.

I really like the interaction that intrigue provides.  It definitely has more than dominion.  Most people say this is just more luck being added to the game and it hurts the concept.  However, I feel it is a good change of pace.  I also like the options on the cards, there are now more hard decisions to be made more often.  Some say this means you don't have to build as good of a deck, you just buy this card and it acts like anything you need it to be at any time.  I disagree and think it just means you now have harder decisions to make during your turn, which is one complaint from dominion.

I don't know if I would suggest intrigue as a stand-alone game.  We played it stand alone at first so we would have a better chance of seeing all the new cards, but I really feel like combining the two really gives the best play.  We usually do 5 random cards from each.  Also, the cards are a little more complex for somebody just learning the game.  For those reasons I'd say get dominion first, but definitely look into getting both, because the two together really make the playing experience the best.

I gave this an 8 rating, because there is too much luck for me to rate it any higher.  My most favorite games have less luck involved and I really think the more strategy involved the better the game is in a lot of cases.  This is a great game and as a expansion to the 2009 spiel des jahres winner, you can't go wrong.

[b]Game Length:[/b] (Short) :star::halfstar::nostar::nostar::nostar: (Long)
[b]Complexity:[/b] (Easy) :star::star::star::nostar::nostar: (Complex)
[b]Accessibility:[/b] (Non-Gamers) :star::star::star::nostar::nostar: (Gamers)
[b]Luck Factor:[/b] (Luck Based) :star::star::halfstar::nostar::nostar: (Strategy Based)
[b]Re-playability:[/b] (Low) :star::star::star::star::star: (High)
[b]Value for Time:[/b] (Waste) :star::star::star::star::star: (Worth)
[b]Recommended # of Players:[/b] 3-5  You can only play more than 4 players if you have both dominion and intrigue.  If you buy this as a standalone you can only go up to 4.

RATING: 8.75
Played once.  This is an expansion to Dominion, and the rules are functionally identical.  As with Dominion, this game is thoughtful yet extremely quick.  

This expansion adds a variety of cards, and the set I played with was extremely well thought out.  There are now cards that are both victory points and action/gold cards.  The set also included a card that gave bonus points for each Dutchy (3 VP card) that the player has; this makes a previously not-very-useful card into a highly sought after one, and opens up a second track to victory.

All in all this seems like a great addition, though I need to play with more of the expansion cards to know.

RATING: 8
Draft and play cards to improve your deck and collect victory cards for most points.

Plays: More than 500, counting online play against humans.
Type: VP engine = a game where you build an engine to collect victory points most efficiently.
Complexity: Light.
# of players: 2-4.
Playing time: 45 mins.
Player interaction: Competition for scarce resources – action and victory cards. Sometimes conflict, which always affects all opponents equally.
Randomness: Low – card draw, but you decide what cards make up your deck.

Replayability: Very high. Often everyone wants to play again immediately. There are millions of variations because the design is modular, so no game is exactly the same. There is also depth to explore.
Fun: High. Making high value hands is fun. Drawing your entire deck with action cards is even more fun. The endless shuffling is not so fun. Intrigue has slightly more fun cards than the base set.
Memorability: High, you’ll remember the wicked combo that you managed to get off that one time to buy three Provinces and a Duchy. You’ll start remembering the less spectacular ones as well after a while, hoping for your pet cards to appear in the Kingdom next time.

Thematic integration: Strained.
Components: Not so good unfortunately. Cards are good quality, but the art is bland.
Expansions: Expansions in order of increasing complexity/fiddlyness: Hinterlands, Cornucopia, Seaside, Prosperity, Dark Ages, Alchemy. Get Hinterlands first.

Who will like this: Family gamers that want to do a bit more thinking.

RATING: 5
Ok, yes. The new cards kick much ass - they add some much needed complexity and interaction missing from the basic game. But the same flaw still exists: a player that focuses on a simple cash-upgrade strategy will almost always outpace a player who is exploring some alternative strategy (ex: Duchy + Duke) offered by the new cards. This is a critical flaw! It means the most efficient path to winning is the most boring and simple, and it invalidates the need to even bother purchasing or playing this expansion. Furthermore, after playing a round of this, the owner who brought it informed me that the THIRD expansion is already announced for ESSEN. It seems this is just a high price-tag version of a CCG now. I will certainly play it if others suggest it - it's a nice social game (reminds me more and more of Skip-Bo or Uno) - but in the end I know I will not be purchasing any new expansions for it.

Without continuing to buy expansion after expansion of this, it starts to feel really rote and uninteresting. It's basically Deck: The Shuffling.

RATING: 9
Had we gone the popularly recommended route of starting with Dominion and then going to Seaside, I might not think as highly of Intrigue. It would have just been a little more variety and perhaps felt a bit redundant with the base set.

But in our case, after playing the original a few times, we went out and got Intrigue and played the shit out of it instead. The cards provide more options and are generally more interactive. We simply got more mileage out of this set on its own than I think we would have gotten from the base set, and I recommend it over the original to non-casual gamers who don't think they'll be introducing Dominion to a lot of new people. After this, Seaside added some nice variety, but the base set already seemed stale.

[i]Note: All our plays are now logged here, even if Intrigue itself contributed no Kingdom cards to the board, though I will continue co-logging plays under new expansions until we get to 100 plays on them. Gotta consolidate these somewhere, and Intrigue > Dominion in our world.[/i]

The introduction of combo victory/action and victory/treasure cards *as well as* the potential to sabotage, swindle, etc. make this a much more complex competitive experience, and new card functions, except for the usual 2-3 blah cards, make fresh strategizing a fun necessity.

Nits: Bridge costs far too little for what it does; overloading on the new combination victory-and cards gets clunky; more buy multipliers and action multipliers would be helpful (but of course, since this can be integrated with original Dominion, you can swap in Festival, Village, Woodcutter, and other option-increasing cards). Masquerade is only fun with three or more players, probably ditto Torturer. Wishing Well is wimpy, Coppersmith is fantastic but only if you have an action multiplier like Shantytown... actually a lot of cards are fantastic but only with Shantytown. Our first thought was also that Pawn costs too little, but considering the power of the Saboteur, it's actually a great idea to make that cost 2.

Picks: Bridge is freaking awesome. Great art, spectacular economic monkey wrenching. Saboteur is the card that makes this game seriously angsty and competitive and fun; in the original, whoever got cards just kept them, and losers knew they were losing, but now ownership is not forever. (Small nit: Trashing as opposed to restoring to buy piles cuts the game off too quickly if you're obeying the if-3-action-cards-are-sold-out-game-over rule, which we don't, but still.) Trading Post gives you a lot of freedom to consolidate copper or switch out cards that aren't as useful later in the game, since you get a silver for trashing 2 cards and can even make money breaking curses. Conspirator is a significant improvement over your vanilla +2 treasure cards; variable function cards like Nobles and Pawns rock (though to maintain the spirit and risk of the game, we keep the rule that you have to declare what functions you're choosing at the time of play); Swindler seems like a great idea until you play it and someone turns up a Province, which might blow the whole game up in your face, which is beautiful.

Actual Problems: Card art in the first edition of Intrigue is definitely not as successful as in the original base game, and there is one actually offensive card: Harem, while technically useful as a combination 2 Victory / 2 Treasure card, has heavy-handedly ethnically stereotyped women lounging around in improbable clothing, and frankly, we know what a harem is, and this is actually a brothel - the treasure points make that clear. Other than that, there is the same dearth of women on the cards as in the original base game (and of course that one had one woman card too: the Witch). We are really hoping the second edition includes things like women on the Nobles card and a conversion of the "Harem" into some kind of gambling den.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
There is absolutely NO reason to play this with more than 4 people. Just split them into two games instead.

Intrigue has many more interesting cards than Dominion. However, I have a complaint about 3 specific cards:

1) Baron
I believe this card is broken. +1 buy is not all that impressive on its own, I understand. However, Baron + Estate is worth essentially 2 silvers, WITH A BUY ATTACHED. It is entirely too easy, with first round Baron and Silver purchases, to stack your deck with excessive amounts of money. This strategy sets up so quickly that most other decks can't keep up. This is ESPECIALLY true in 2 player games.

Update (3/25/13): Not broken, just incredibly solid.

2) Swindler
This card makes for excessively unfun games. An early Swindler essentially means that everyone else's copper quickly becomes curses, while you get an extra +2 credit. It quickly spirals into a "I'm going to swindle your Swindler" mess.

Update(3/25/13): Still hate this card. It's still unfun.

3) Saboteur
Essentially the same problem here as the Swindler, except it costs 5 and doesn't actually get you anything other than messing with your opponent's decks. Not quite as bad, but can ruin games, considering this card CAN hit provinces.

Update (3/25/13): Considering this card doesn't advance your position, I consider it a waste of a buy. A well-tuned deck can outrace a Saboteur pretty easily.


Favorite Card (3/25/13): Minion

RATING: 7.5
Dominion is a deck building game where all players start with a bit of money and a few victory points and use those cards to "purchase" additional cards for their deck from a common pool of cards.  I like it quite a bit, as it has a lot of the feel of Magic but is much more accessible to new players.  The intrigue set of cards is interesting, but unlike the original set there are no cards that allow for directly cursing another player.  It can still be done through cards like Masquerade or Swindler, but you have to get lucky rather than outright curse someone.  If I had a complaint it is that the game can be fairly solitary.  Even though you are playing with other people, there are often games where you are simply interacting with your own deck rather than with the other players at the table.  Part of the joy I get from playing tabletop games is that interaction with other players, and Dominion isn't very good at fostering that interaction.  That is a minor quibble, though, as it is an enjoyable strategy card game that is easy to pickup and fun to replay.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This adds to the original 25 cards that comes with Dominion.  I found these cards upped the interaction between you and your opponents, but I am not so sure that is a great thing in this game.  At least I do not like how they implemented it.  In this game if your opponents decide to start attacking you, you wind up picking up a card that defends you against these attacks.  It just starts adding cards into both of your decks just for the sake of interaction.

I do not hate it, but I have since traded this expansion away.  I feel that Dominion is more fun without worrying about the added complexity/annoyance of interaction.  Plus, I like other Dominion expansion more and the amount that I play it, I do not need all of them.

RATING: 9
[i]As an expansion[/i], it's a must-buy, and probably at its best when combined with the base game. About half of the cards are very clever. The rest vary from less interesting to weak. 

Adds a lot more decisions, interaction, and card text, which means that turns take a longer time now, and cards are more difficult to figure out. Which is even more strange considering that they have managed to do it correctly on the Ironworks and Tribute cards anyway. While the original [gameid=36218] is very accessible and plays quickly even with beginners and non-gamers, I'll probably try to avoid playing this expansion with those groups or slow players. 

[i]As a complete game[/i], it's not as elegant as the original [gameid=36218].

RATING: 8
If you don't think the base Dominion set provides enough conflict, this is the expansion for you.  Intrigue includes more attacks, more ways to mess with your opponents, and more ways to interact.  For some, this will be a distinct downer since the conflict "feels" wrong for a game in this genre.  For others, it's a nice change of pace.

I've found that I don't like mixing more than two of the Dominion sets, though.  Throw three together and instead of "flavor" you get "a mess."  But the ability to mix & match provides lots and lots of replay capacity in a relatively short, easy to learn game with great depth.

RATING: 7.5
It's ok. Definitely adds more to the interactive gameplay than the original, even though there seems to be quite heavy cards now, and if you don't use the pre-selected decks you might get totally weird and unplayable combinations...

Also I've ran into a certain pattern while playing - from 10 action decks on the table, more than 3 are usually not even touched. Makes you wonder if there are the few really usable cards and rest are just the filling or the frosting on the cake...

Still I wonder the card design - of course now it's impossible to change anything since they have to be compatible backwards, but what is the idea of the backside being symmetric, but the fronts still need to be right way to be able to read the texts? One of the biggest and annoying design flaws I think in a game where you need to shuffle cards all the time, and spend another minute of turning the cards correctly in your hand...

Good, but not great. Still suggest Evolution Earth: Cataclysm for a different approach of similar gamestyle. Much, much more deeper and more tied to the theme also...

RATING: 8
Like the Dominion base game, this has an excellent gameplay and is very easy for first-time players to pick up. Very replayable due to the different selections of available cards, most of which are quite balanced (I've seen the vast majority of the cards used successfully in different strategies). More of a '2nd release' than an expansion, Intrigue comes with the Treasure and Victory cards allowing it to be played independently from the original. Compared with Dominion, there are fewer cards that give you lots of actions and buys, meaning the gameplay can be slightly 'cagier' - whether this is a good or bad thing depends on what you like!

RATING: 10
Dominion took a path to a more complex and deeper game with Intrigue. You have choices on cards, hybrid cards and more interesting attack cards. Thus the strategies are not that straigt forward anymore. Average game length is probably a bit longer than with base Dominion alone, but I don´t mind it when I get a more interesting game to play.

Opposed to some other fellow gamers opininons I think that Dominion is very dynamic and variable. It is not that easy to figure out what combination works better than others from the available 10 cards each game. Also playing with different people means games will have different flow and strategies used. Replay value is extremely high.

update: after 86 plays, this game has officialy gone gold for me. I just can´t get enough of this. Rating 9 -> 10

RATING: 6
Maybe I'm not using this expansion right, but it seemed to slow down the base game quite a bit. By that I mean that the attacks slowed engine building and the decreased number of "extra action" cards tended to make the turns simpler and less interesting. I think some of the cards would be very interesting, but as a spice. Supposedly this is a playable game (ie., playable without owning the base game) but a bit slower and meaner than base Dominion. I like the modified green cards which give a blend of points and powers. It's nice to be able to have a points card that isn't complete deadweight in terms of play, but I would call this an expansion to be used sparingly to add to the base game, rather than calling it a playable alternate base game. It is decidedly not in the same league as the original base game when used alone.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Below are my comments on Dominion.  Intrigue is just more of the same.  If you love Dominion, you'll probably love the added variety in Intrigue.

[q="rayito2702"]This is an okay game. Players start out with a set deck of cards. On a turn, players play what cards they can and discard the rest. Cards provide points, money and other types of powers. Throughout the game players use their existing cards to acquire new ones. If properly chosen the new cards will combine to produce additional fun combinations of card play and more points.

Game play is simple to the point of being simplistic. It's the card combos that add what spice there is to the game. There's a few "screw your neighbor" cards, but mostly players will be racing to get the desirable cards into their deck as fast as possible.

Basically this is your standard Efficiency Engine game built around a novel deck building mechanism. For me, a novel mechanism does not a good game make. On one hand the game is light and fluffy and takes hardly any time at all to play. On the other it strives for complexity in the card combos. It goes by too fast to enjoy what complexity there is, while being too fiddly and full of pieces to justify the quick playing time. It's sort of like listening to Beethoven's fifth sped up to twice the normal speed.

Maybe if I played it enough so that I could process the card combos and endless shuffling without thinking the game would become more interesting. But its currently not interesting enough to devote that kind of time to.

It desperately needs card protectors since some cards will get worn out much faster than others. The graphic design of the cards leave much to be desired. The card backs are atrocious and the art, while not bad, is just generic fantasy and I'm sick of generic fantasy.[/q]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
An interesting set of cards, like:
Bridge (reducing costs of cards to buy is great, the combo with multiple throne rooms or king's courts can be incredible!)
Duke (all of a sudden going for duchies can be profitable!)
Ironworks (gain a card costing 4 can be powerful if you draw a victory/action card like great hall or island. A very quick way to run out of 3 stacks!)
Nobles (one of my favourites. Gives you vp, and then either extra cards or extra actions, making it always useful!)
Saboteur (the most frustrating dominion card ever, especially when someone sabotages your colonies or provinces)
Steward (great variability, +2 cards, +2 coins or 2 trashes, works great with nobles in this set too)
Torturer (frustrating, do you discard or take a curse. How about getting this 3 times in a row? aargh!)
Upgrade (an awesome (free, as it is +1 actions +1 card) way to get rid of estates in exchange for silvers!)

And also minion, mining village and masquerade are awesome! Great set!

RATING: 10
The first Dominion expansion does contain a small number of highly situational or even borderline-useless cards (chiefly Scout, but I think Coppersmith, at least, usually falls in this category), but it is still a must-have for all Dominion fans. Many powerful and interesting cards (Minion especially), and also cheap and flexible cards (Steward, and especially Pawn). Also - and this will be a downside for many, not least my wife, who hates this expansion - some of the cruelest attacks in the game (Swindler, Torturer, Saboteur). There is nothing especially complicated here, and Intrigue is undoubtedly more interesting than the base set when considered as standalone games, but I would still recommend new players start with the base set, as many of the Intrigue cards require some experience with the game to know what to do with quickly or effectively.

RATING: 6
Added much-needed diversity to Dominion, but I personally find a lot of the cards in Intrigue shift time away from the part I find most satisfying, which is the deck building part. There's a lot more going on with tactical card play with all of the options available. The attack cards are very nasty and can totally wreak havoc on whatever you're trying to build, forcing you to adapt. They can also force the game to end with the three-stacks-gone rule, which makes the game much longer.

It's a very interesting addition to Dominion, but games with a lot of Intrigue cards tend to run long for my tastes and drag out. When mixed with the base set, though, there's not as much chaos. The versatility of some of the Intrigue cards comes out instead of being unnecessary complexity. I much prefer the mixed version.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Dominion for the Ameritrash folks. Nastier attacks. More randomness. Bring it on.

I luuurve Secret Chamber, even though most strategy players don't like this card. At the beginning of the game, you use it to buy a 4-gold card, even though the rest of your hand has coppers and estates. In the middle of the game, you wave it around even though it doesn't stop an attack, then set up your hand for the next draw. It's best to have a strong hand each turn, but SC at least can convert two middling hands into a weak hand this turn (which gets attacked) and a strong hand next. Since it affects the top card of your deck, you also get to gloat when someone attacks the top card of your deck -- keep their hands off your Gold and show them an Estate! If attacked, you can even put the SC back on top of your deck for next turn, if you happen to know what cards are left in your deck!

Anyway, for OP:
* Euro: Dominion, Prosperity, Seaside.
* Ameritrash: Intrigue, Hinterlands, Guilds and Cornucopia, Adventure

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
After a number of plays, this brings Dominion into the realm of "terrific" for me. If the base game was too vanilla for you, problem solved. If the cards seemed too similar, problem solved. This is one of the best expansions ever released, and one that is necessary for any fan of the base game.

The highest compliment that can be paid is that it changes the feel of the game without adding any rules weight at all. The game feels a little more aggressive (though interaction still is pretty low) and just a bit more thematic (though it's still very abstract), but it's still Dominion, just taken in a different direction.

*edit* This is the better base set for Dominion, but it has suffered the same fate of just sitting on the shelf. It has value, but I have other deckbuilders that I like more.

RATING: 9
Lots of fun new kooky cards (although, I'm not a fan of one card in particular).  Really, this is just more great Dominion crack.  There is no reason not to get this if you want to switch stuff up a bit.  The nice thing is that this will come with the money and VP cards again, so people can start here, or for people like me that would like to expand it to more players -- this will allow for 5 or 6 or will allow two groups to play this simultaneously.

The only reason that I don't give this a 10 is that there are two cards that I don't really enjoy playing with. 

First, The Saboteur is just intolerable.  It stretches the game out to no rewarding end.  If there is no defensive card available it is even worse.  Blech.  Every time someone plays the card you essentially lose one turn of builds.  This gets old really fast.

The second, The Minion, while not a terrible offender, it just irritating when people keep having to discard their whole hand.  You don't even want to look at your hand until it is your turn.  So annoying.

RATING: 8
I like to call this "Base Set #2".  Like the base Dominion set this includes a bunch of standard utility cards that would be good in any Kingdom setup.  Nothing fancy but they work great and can be building blocks to great combos and interesting plays when combined with some of the other more inventive cards in future sets.

The most interesting addition in this set were the dual victory - action/treasure cards that allowed you to collect victory points and still have a functional card when you drew it into your hand.  Also, just the fact that this adds 25 new Kingdom cards AND an additional set of basic treasures/victory cards/curses makes this a hit.  New cards (as long as they work in the context of the  game) are always a boon for deck-builders to keep them fresh and giving players the resources to play two games or up to a 6-player single game makes this a must-buy for any Dominion fan.

RATING: 7.5
This game is... well... intriguing.  But I'll get the negatives out of the way before I jump into the positive aspects.  The main reason I will not purchase this game/expansion is that they released it in a big box, full game format instead of a smaller, cheaper set of expansion cards.  I can see why they would want to cater to those who wished to make "Dominion" playable with more than 4 players (and while I haven't tried it, I can see how that might work out fairly well since downtime is so minimal in this game), but I'd rather they had released the extra money and VP cards as a separate expansion too.  Also, the light blue and red colour scheme is just as atrocious as the original game, and the artwork rides the same fine line between kind of neat and fairly cheesy.  However, to focus on more positive things, it's always nice to increase the number of different card options, particularly when several of those cards involve interaction with other players.  The coolest thing about the new cards are the ones that have combined action/VP effects, such as the "Harem" card (now THAT is some pretty awful artwork...).  Overall, I find that the negatives balance out the positives to maintain a rating that's identical to the original game - it's still a very enjoyable gaming experience.  Game design: 4/5  Personal enjoyment: 3.5/5  Total: 7.5/10

RATING: 6
I bought this one on a whim, just so that we could have a 5-player game with someone else's base set. I enjoy Dominion, but I think it's a bit over-hyped. It's a good game, but I can only play a hand or two before I'm ready to move on. I tend to stick with a straight-forward "get as much gold as possible, and cards that allow me to draw more" and I win as much as I lose -- no matter what combination of cards are in play. I think this is one of the reasons that I don't like the game. Sure, you can come up with elaborate strategies and combinations... but why? You can do just as well by filling your deck with gold.

RATING: 8
Sleevat Arcane Tinmen Large
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The notion of the modular expansion - where you have a number of small new elements to use in whatever combination you wish - Dominion expansions are the epitome.

25 new modules to mix and match!

The problem is that few of those modules, here and in other sets, really change how you approach playing the game. Having Great Halls in a setup, or Wishing Wells, or Trading Posts doesn't require any real difference in approach. That's true of basically every card in this particular set, which is conservative in part since it can be used stand-alone.

There is one inevitable wrinkle when playing with new cards: that's in working out if they're priced favourably or not. It doesn't take much, though, to figure out that Scout isn't incredible in most setups (experience of the card in play hardly seems necessary in this and other cases). And, given the variable value of Dominion cards (a plus action card is more valuable if its the only one available, for instance), good play is based on evaluation from principle rather than practice (i.e. having a broad plan before the game even starts). So you have situations where a new card or two are on offer, but you'd reduce your chance of winning were you to buy them. That's not much fun.

RATING: 8.25
Intrigue includes cards that allow players to win without adopting a big money strategy, while including some nice utility cards that aren't overpowered. Baron and Minion can completely change the way the game is played. As a result, I feel that this is a slightly more interesting stand-alone set than the core Dominion game.

The attack cards in Intrigue are stronger than their core counterparts, while the protection is lacking. Swindler can be especially devastating in the absence of thinner cards.

Being able to accommodate 5-6 players is an added bonus for owning both sets.
