RATING: 9
One of the games I've played most of the times with my friends. The game that has been preferred as "first to play" with my friends and people to whom this was the first ever experience in the board game world. Super easy to teach. Explaining the basics and how the game functions might take as little as 10 minutes (I've managed to teach it in 5). The only you cannot teach is the winning strategy and card plays/actions. How to utilize your hand more efficiently is a learning process. For me it took less than 10 plays to work out my own strategy and how to dirsupt opponents' game and I can tell you I am surely not an advanced gamer.

The only thing that I and my friends changed right after the first game was the selection of kingdom cards. We use ten decks with ten different kingdom cards in each deck. So in one deck you have a Duke, Minion, Secret Chamber, Torturer, Scout, Mining Village, Well, Baron, Bridge, Nobles. In another - Swindler, Saboteur, Harem, Shanty Town, Coppersmith, Bridge, Nobles, Ironworks, Upgrade, Torturer

That way the game gets more diverse and interesting. All other rules though remain the same. The only drawback (quite seriously impacting the play) is the time it takes to complete a single play. If with the original rules you can manage a play in about 20 minutes or even a bit less then with the altered rules it may even take up to an hour to finish.

Otherwise the game is excellent and all the expansions it has just adds up to numereous card comincations and options you have to play your hand and stack up the deck.

Excellent game for a starter or even the very first purchase of a board game.

RATING: 8.9
the theme intrigue is good for Dominion, and the translation into cards is good

Intrigue really adds a layer to Dominion gameplay, because some cards have several possible effect to choose from, and much more player interaction than the base game, as the name implies. the cards balance, however, isn't really good : some cards are too good, while some are hard to use. also, the playing time increased because there are many choices in cards. the 5-6P variant is okay, but not really recommended, the game is still best with 4P

the artwork style is diversed, the lines in several cards is too thick that they looked more like drawing than picture. i prefer Dominion's artwork than Intrigue's

Intrigue is not newbie-friendly, compared to Dominion, the card effects are rather complex to explain. of course i rate this as an expansion, not as base game. overall i rate it 9- . simply put, i prefer Dominion than Intrigue

RATING: 5
Sat down to a couple games at the local game store. Intrigue is a welcome improvement on the base game; most notably in that some action cards offer you choices, so there is presumably more of a decision to be made when playing actions rather than it just being automatic. Still, I found decisions fairly obvious and didn't find the experience fundamentally different. With just skimming the new cards and going with my old Dominion habits I was still able to win every game. In the end, I think this will appeal to those who are still high on Dominion and want more. For someone like me who played the game obsessively online and then burned out there's nothing here compelling enough to reawaken my interest (I'd play again a couple times just to see all the action cards but that's probably it).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
If you liked the original game, it's probably safe to say that you'll like the expansion.  It adds cards that do new things, change some things, and make you rethink the best strategy toward playing a given game.  The great thing about Dominion is that the approach you take to playing any given game differs depending on how the different cards work together.  If you like that aspect of the game, and are looking for newer, more interesting ways to apply that principle to the game, get it.  Most of the cards, though, add a lot of direct interaction, and also makes the game far more chaotic than I like.  I know that a lot of complaints about the original game was that it wasn't interactive enough, but the Intrigue cards take it far beyond what I enjoy about the game.  So much of it is ridiculously out of your control, and it becomes ultimately frustrating.

11 plays: 2 players
4 plays: 3 players
8 plays: 4 players
3 plays: 5 players
1 play: 6 players

It's a very good game, but lacks horribly in theme. The theme could be non-existent, but it doesn't really matter, as the game has interesting and simple mechanics. Having only Intrigue, there isn't that much fighting with other players, which can be a problem if you're into this kind of gameplay.
Also, the game does tire after some time, especially when usually played with 2 players. It's very simple, but at the same time, not immersing enough to make me want to play again and again. If you've never played card-based games, this may definitely be for you. Otherwise - you might wanna check out something else.

和皇舆争霸系列其它众多扩充不同的是，“阴谋”不仅是系列中的第一个扩充，而且为唯一可以完全独立于基础而独自游戏的扩充，如果和原基础搭配更是支持最多6人玩家同时参与游戏。“阴谋”中加入了全新的要数，比如双属性卡牌，多选能力行动卡，更多玩家互动等，让游戏的变化和耐玩性得到了更高的升华。
